<div><span style=""font-weight: 700;"">Innervation
</span></div>
<div>Clavicular part: Innervation is via the lat-
eral pectoral nerve, lateral cord, upper
trunk, and roots C5, C6.
</div>
<div>Sternocostal part: Innervation is via the
lateral and medial pectoral nerves,
lateral and medial cords, middle and
lower trunks, and roots C7, C8, T1.&nbsp;</div>

<div><b style="""">Biceps Femoris (long &amp; Short, Semimembranosus,
and Semitendinosus)</b></div>
<div>Nerve:<span style=""font-weight: 700;"">&nbsp;</span>{{c2::sciatic nerve&nbsp;<u>Tibial division</u> &amp;&nbsp;<u>common peroneal division</u>&nbsp;(to
short head of biceps femoris)::2 + caveat}}&nbsp;&nbsp;<br></div><div>Roots: {{c1::L5,&nbsp;S1, S2::3}} no major&nbsp;</div><div><img src=""paste-d1a03f3f3d151114b1f6a5502ad8f5afb9cf45d9.jpg""><br></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>"	"<div>Division: Anterior (mainly save for posterior biceps short)<br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-04-10 at 7.14.26 PM.png""><br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2023-03-18 at 11.18.06 AM.png""><br></div><div><img src=""paste-4e5ac4b42d91022c28e23db95bea0a3bacf72345.jpg""><br></div>"										
"{{c1::<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">de</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">myelination</span>}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">is an injury to sheath of the nerve (but the axon remains intact.)</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">translates to <u>slower signal conduction</u> (onset/peak latency +/- duration) along the axon.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"	"may present as decrease in <u>amplitude</u> if a conduction block is present&nbsp;<div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_14.png""><br></div>"										
"<div>Failure of an&nbsp;AP&nbsp;to propagate past an area of demyelination (along healthy axons)</div><div>is known as&nbsp;{{c1::<strong>conduction block</strong>.}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It can present as a {{c2::&gt;20% - &gt;50%::%range2#'s}} drop in&nbsp;{{c3::CMAP&nbsp;amplitude}} with stim.&nbsp;{{c4::across the area of injury or L/R comparison::location 2}}<br></div>"	"ex. a type of severe focal demyelination (ulnar tunnel, saturday night palsy)<div><div>
<div>
</div></div></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-21 at 10.05.53 AM.png""><br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-21 at 10.05.19 AM.png""><br></div>"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>demyelination affects</b>&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">the <u>speed</u> of signal conduction along a nerve</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">thus&nbsp;</span>NCS's (CMAP and SNAP)&nbsp;</div><div><u>parameters effected include<font color=""#333333""><span style=""caret-color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">:</span></font></u></div><div>{{c1::o/p&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">latency</span>}}</div><div>{{c1::CV}}</div><div>{{c1::duration (temporal dispersion)}}<br></div></div>"	"<div><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-21 at 10.18.40 AM.png""><br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-22 at 4.29.26 PM.png""><br></div>"										
"{{c1::Axonal}} injuries<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;affect the amplitude on nerve conduction waveform</span>"	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-21 at 10.25.28 AM.png"">"										
"{{c1::Axonal Degeneration}}:<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;A nerve injury that begins in a “</span><span style=""font-style: italic; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">dying back</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">” fashion and affects the nerve distally and ascends proximally</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div>{{c1::Wallerian Degeneration}}:<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">A nerve injury that&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">degenerates distally. The nerve segment proximal to the injury site is essentially intact</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_18.png"">"										
"<b>{{c1::Collateral sprouting}}</b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is repair in which a neurite sends off axons of an intact motor unit&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">and innervates muscle fibers of an injured motor unit</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><u><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">results in MUAP changes&nbsp;</span>(evidnece of chronic injury):</u></div><div>{{c2::polyphasic waveforms}}&nbsp;&nbsp;<br></div></div><div>{{c2::increased duration}}&nbsp;<br></div><div>{{c2::increased amplitude}}<br></div>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">- sprouts connect with smaller terminal branches, thinner myelin, and weaker&nbsp;</span>NMJs<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">- increasing size of MU territory</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">- motor units fire with poor synchronicity</span></div><div><img src=""paste-55366423412739.jpg"" style=""color: rgb(255, 0, 0);""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_19.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><br></div>"										
"{{c1::Axonal regrowth}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is a process of repair in which the nerve regrows down its original path</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">It will travel approximately&nbsp;</span>{{c2::1 mm}}/d<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;or&nbsp;</span>{{c3::1 in./}}<span style=""font-style: italic; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">mo</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">if the supporting connective tissue remains intact.&nbsp; </span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">With reinnervation, low-amplitude, long-duration, and polyphasic potentials known as&nbsp;</span><span style=""font-style: italic; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">nascent potentials</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;are formed.</span><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_20.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>Sunderland Classification</b></span><div><font color=""#333333""><b><br></b></font><div><table><tbody><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><strong>TYPE 1</strong></td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">{{c1::Conduction block (<u>neuropraxia</u>)::2}}</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><strong>TYPE 2</strong></td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">{{c2::Axonal injury (<u>axonotmesis</u>)::2}}</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><strong>TYPE 3</strong></td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Type 2 + {{c3::Endoneurium}} injury</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><strong>TYPE 4</strong></td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Type 3 + {{c4::Perineurium}} injury</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><strong>TYPE 5</strong></td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Type 4 + {{c5::Epineurium injury (<u>neurotmesis</u>)::2}}</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_21.png""><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_1.png""><br><div><br></div></div>"										
"{{c1::Anodal Block}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is A theoretical local block that occurs when reversing the stimulator’s cathode and anode.&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">This hyperpolarizes the nerve, thus inhibiting the production of an action potential</span></div>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_28.png"">"										
"{{c1::Supramaximal stimulus}}<strong>&nbsp;</strong><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">stim. intensity 20% above the max stimulus to generate an AP (typically used for&nbsp;</span>NCS<font color=""#333333"">)</font><div><font color=""#333333""><br></font></div><div><div><u>stimulus intensity set too {{c2::high}}</u>&nbsp;</div><div>- {{c4::Altered waveforms (spreads through tissues beyond surface electrodes)}}</div><div>- Amplitudes {{c4::remain unchanged}}</div><div><br></div><div><div><u><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">stimulus intensity set too&nbsp;</span>{{c2::low}}</u><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">- falsely&nbsp;</span>{{c3::lower amplitude}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">- falsely&nbsp;</span>{{c3::prolonged latency}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><br></div></div></div>"	"<img src=""nerve-conduction-study-medical-treatment-services-500x500.jpg"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">process of&nbsp;</span><span style=""font-style: italic; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">averaging</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;improves the&nbsp;</span>{{c1::Signal to Noise Ratio (S:N)}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;by a factor that is the square root of the number of averages performed.&nbsp;</span>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">This averaging process extracts the desired neurophysiologic signal from larger <u>noise and interference</u> signals</span><div><br></div><div>S:N= {<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Signal amplitude × √# of averages performed} /&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Noise amplitude</span><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Interference = unwanted signals occurring from outside the system being studied</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Noise = unwanted signals occurring from within the system (eg.&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">electrical outlets, fluorescent lights)</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_66.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"										
<b>Stimulus Artifact</b><div><b><br></b><div>This is a defect seen at the time the stimulus is applied to the skin and represents current spread to the electrode. It can be minimized by</div><div><br></div><div>Appropriate: {{c2::ground and stimulator (anode and cathode)::equipment factor 2}} placement</div><div><br></div><div>{{c1::Cleansing the skin from dirt, perspiration, and lotions::pt factor}}</div></div>	"<img src=""https://www.researchgate.net/publication/328964432/figure/fig5/AS:757401594654720@1557590020218/Combination-of-M-wave-and-stimulation-artifact-for-creating-semi-synthetic-signals-for.ppm"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">A grid is projected on the screen with the horizontal axis representing&nbsp;</span>{{c1::sweep speed (<i>msec</i>)::name, unit}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;and the vertical axis representing&nbsp;</span>{{c2::sensitivity (<i>mV</i>)::name, unit}}<span style=""font-style: italic; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;or gain</span><div><span style=""font-style: italic; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div>each cube is a {{c3::division}}</div>"	"<div>&nbsp;&nbsp;<img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-21 at 6.27.59 PM.png""></div><div><img src=""F1.large-5523e0741107c3a7a22d174ea876013d3212bb5d.jpg""><br></div><div><img src=""image2.png""><br></div>"										
"{{c1::Onset/distal latency (CMAP)}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is the time required for an electrical stimulus to initiate an evoked potential (fastest axon)</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div>{{c1::Peak latency (SNAP)}}<strong>&nbsp;</strong><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is the time for </span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">the majority of the axons&nbsp;</span></div>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_34.png"">"										
"{{c1::conduction velocity}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is the <u>speed</u> an impulse travels along a nerve&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">primarily dependent on the integrity of the&nbsp;</span>{{c2::myelin}}</div><div><br></div><div>Normal values are&nbsp;generally&nbsp;&gt;{{c3::50}}&nbsp;m/sec in the <u>upper limbs</u> and &gt;{{c3::40}}&nbsp;m/sec in the <u>lower limbs</u><br></div>"	"<div>It can be decreased with nerve injury and from technical factors.&nbsp;<br></div><div><br></div><div>It should remain <u>normal</u> even in severe axonal injuries, as&nbsp;NCSs&nbsp;record the velocity of <font color=""#fc0006"">fastest surviving nerve fibers</font></div><div><img src=""M4MwkNraEuXR8h-Y_Nbf2VT-v4pzfl15yDjdexQg0IZn-b2wMVgf1n0RUG-6WsAii-FFqUlpT8As_iUv_6UkEu6FT8DfCgOt8KOspkrymTDEWI1CUis.png""><br></div>"										
"<div><b>EMG/NCS Conduction Velocity</b></div><div><br></div>CV<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">for a newborn is 50% that of an adult. At 1 year, it is 80% that of an adult. It is equal to an adult by&nbsp;</span>{{c1::3–5::#~#}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;years</span><div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">After the&nbsp;</span>{{c2::5th}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;decade, the&nbsp;</span>CV<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;decreases&nbsp;</span>{{c3::1–2::range}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;m/sec per decade</span><br></div>"											
"{{c1::Amplitude}}&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">reflects the number of activated&nbsp;<u>muscle fibers</u>&nbsp;or</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;<u>sensory nerve</u> fibers</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div>CMAP (or SNAP) {{c1::amplitude::same}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;reductions are due to injury to&nbsp;</span>{{c2::axons}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">(typical axonal neuropathy), other causes </span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">include conduction block,&nbsp;</span>NMJ<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;disorders, and myopathies</span><br><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_34.png""><br></div>"										
"{{c1::duration::NCS parameter}} is&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">measured from the initial deflection from baseline to the first baseline crossing.</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">it is a measure of&nbsp;</span>{{c2::synchrony}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;of the sensory nerve fibers and&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">individual muscle </span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">fibers firing</span></div>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_34.png"">"										
"{{c1::Temporal dispersion}}&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">reflects the range of conduction velocities of the fastest and slowest nerve fibers.</span>"	"<div>ex. segmental demeylination 2/2 GBS, CIDP</div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_35.png""><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-22 at 4.29.26 PM.png""><br></div>"										
"<div><b>{{c1::Phase Cancellation}}</b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;=&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">when stimulated, the&nbsp;</span>APs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;of one axon may be <u>out of sync</u> with neighboring ones</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>when comparing a&nbsp;</span><u>{{c4::proximal to distal}}</u><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><u>&nbsp;stimulation</u>, a </span><font color=""#064aff"">drop in amplitude</font><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""> and increase in duration occurs (nl.)</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">amplitude drop of&nbsp;</span>{{c2::50%::%}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is considered normal when recording a proximal&nbsp;</span><u>SNAP</u><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">amplitude drop of&nbsp;</span>{{c3::15%::%}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">is considered normal when recording a proximal</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;<u>CMAP</u></span></div>"	"<div>Caveat: <font color=""#fc0006"">DROP <u>only in MOTOR</u> NCS</font> ""sensory to small to count""&nbsp;</div><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_36.png""><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Sensory—</span>SNAP<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;phase cancellation. Open arrows indicate stimulation of the nerve distally; the phases from the individual&nbsp;</span>SNAPs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;summate. Closed arrows indicate stimulation of the nerve <u>proximally</u>; with the increased distance, the <b>phases separate enough</b> by the time they reach the recording electrodes to summate less or <b>even cancel</b>.</span><br></div><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_37.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Motor—</span>CMAP<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;phase cancellation. Open arrows indicate stimulation of the nerve distally resulting in the discharge of two&nbsp;</span>MUAPs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;that produce a potential with twice the size. Closed arrows indicate stimulation of the nerve<u> proximally</u>, resulting in two&nbsp;</span><b>MUAPs</b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>&nbsp;that still summate</b> in phase <b>because of the long duration of the&nbsp;</b></span><b>MUAPs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">’ negative phases.</span></b><br></div>"										
"SNAPs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;are <u>normal</u> in&nbsp;</span>{{c1::Pre-ganglionic::pre/post}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;injury</span>"	"<strong>Postganglionic injury:</strong><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;results in Wallerian degeneration of <u>both</u> motor and sensory axons.&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">CMAP</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;and&nbsp;</span>SNAP<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;responses are diminished or absent.&nbsp; </span><font color=""#0548ff"">peripheral neuropathy&nbsp;</font></div><div><font color=""#333333""><br></font><div><strong>Preganglionic injury:</strong><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;allows the peripheral sensory fibers to remain in contact with their cell body.&nbsp;</span></div><div><font color=""#333333"">SNAPs are normal (</font><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">despite clinical sensory abnormalities) </span><font color=""#0548ff"">Radiculopathy</font><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><font color=""#333333""><br></font><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_38.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div></div></div>"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">active and reference pickup should be&nbsp;</span>{{c1::&gt; 4:: &gt;/&lt;/#}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;cm apart.&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Less than this distance will alter the waveform parameters by&nbsp;</span>{{c2::decreasing::inceasing/decreasing}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;them all</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Save for&nbsp;</span>{{c3::onset latency}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;which will still be normal&nbsp;</span></div>"	"<table><tbody><tr><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><img src=""9780826134578_ufig1.png"" style=""font-weight: 400; text-align: start;""><br>PARAMETERS</th><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><br><br>CHANGE</th></tr></tbody><tbody><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Peak latency</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Decreased</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Amplitude</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Decreased</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Duration</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Decreased</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Rise time</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Decreased</td></tr></tbody></table><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_39.png""><br></div>"

"<strong>EMG MUAP&nbsp;recruitment pattern follows: ""The rule of&nbsp;</strong>{{c1::5's}}<strong>""</strong>"	"<div>The onset frequency of the first&nbsp;MUAP&nbsp;begins at approximately <font color=""#0014ff"">5 Hz</font>. To generate more force, the&nbsp;FR&nbsp;and recruitment of more motor units must be increased.<br></div><div><br></div><div>When the&nbsp;FR&nbsp;reaches approximately <font color=""#0014ff"">10 Hz</font>, a second&nbsp;MUAP&nbsp;begins at approximately <font color=""#0014ff"">5 Hz</font>.</div><div><br></div><div>When the first&nbsp;MUAP&nbsp;reaches a rate of <font color=""#0014ff"">15 Hz</font>, the second should be at 10 Hz and a third will begin at 5 Hz.</div><div><br></div><div>As more force is needed, the&nbsp;FR&nbsp;of the first may reach 20 Hz, the second 15 Hz, the third 10 Hz, and a fourth will begin at approximately 5 Hz.</div>"										
"{{c1::Early recruitment::recruitment pattern}}&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">most commonly seen in <u>myopathic</u> conditions that result in a loss of muscle fibers</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">.&nbsp;</span>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">This loss causes less force to be generated per motor unit. Thus, more motor units must now be called upon</span><div><font color=""#333333""><br></font><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">abnormally early firing of many&nbsp;</span>MUAPs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;with a mild contraction</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-28 at 1.39.57 PM.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div></div>"

"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">F-waves:&nbsp;</span>{{c1::Not::are / are not}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;sensitive / specific for a radiculopathy.&nbsp;</span>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Muscles have more than one root innervation, which can result in a normal latency</span>"										
"EMG<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;for Dx r<u>adiculopathy</u></span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">abnormal findings in&nbsp;</span>{{c1::two or more::#}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;muscles innervated by the same&nbsp;</span>{{c2::spinal nerve root}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;but different&nbsp;</span>{{c2::peripheral nerves}}&nbsp;&nbsp;</div>"											
"EMG<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;for Dx r<u>adiculopathy</u></span><div><font color=""#333333""><u><br></u></font><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Ideally,&nbsp;</span>{{c1::6}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;muscles (</span>{{c1::5}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;peripheral muscles +&nbsp;</span>{{c2::paraspinals}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">) should be evaluated</span></div></div>"	"<div>if one of the six muscles is abnormal, then further muscles should be evaluated.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>A priority is placed on including weak muscles in the evaluation</div><div><img src=""multifidi-cropped-300x240.jpg""><br></div>"										
"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>EMG Radiculopathy Dx</b></span></div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>Classically,&nbsp;</span>{{c1::FIBs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;or&nbsp;</span>PSWs::2}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;found in&nbsp;</span>{{c2::2::#}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;different muscles innervated by different peripheral nerves but same spinal root.&nbsp;</span>"											
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">EMG Radiculopathy Dx</span><br><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>Fibs and Sharps</b> may <u>NOT</u> be found if: the lesion is:&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div>{{c1::demyelinating}}</div><div>{{c2::pure sensory}}</div><div>{{c3::chronic}}</div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">incomplete or missed by random sampling</span></div>"	recall that fibs and sharps are assoc with axonal loss<div><br></div><div>EMG evaluates muscle fibers; not sensory nerves&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>nl. if reinnervation already occured</div>										
"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>Somatosensory Evoked Potential</b>&nbsp;</span></div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>study evaluates&nbsp;</span>{{c1::time-locked}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;responses of the nervous system to an&nbsp;</span>{{c2::external stimulus}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">.&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">SSEP's represent the function of the&nbsp;</span>{{c3::DCML}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;pathway using afferent potentials</span></div>"	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">theoretically evaluate the&nbsp;<u>sensory</u>&nbsp;component of the&nbsp;</span>PNS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;and&nbsp;</span>CNS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">.&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">DX dz of&nbsp;</span>CNS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;(brain, brainstem, spinal cord) as well as of dorsal nerve roots and peripheral nerves&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Abnormal results present immediately</span></div></div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_51.png"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">SSEP's initiated by a repetitive&nbsp;</span>{{c1::submaximal::intensity}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;stimulation of a sensory nerve, mixed nerve, or dermatome,&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">and is recorded from the&nbsp;</span>{{c2::spine}} or {{c2::scalp}}</div>"	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">theoretically evaluate the&nbsp;<u>sensory</u>&nbsp;component of the&nbsp;</span>PNS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;and&nbsp;</span>CNS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">.&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">DX dz of&nbsp;</span>CNS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;(brain, brainstem, spinal cord) as well as of dorsal nerve roots and peripheral nerves&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Abnormal results present immediately</span></div></div><img src=""1951_SEP_450.jpg"">"										
"<b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Somatosensory evoked potential (</span>SSEP</b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>)</b>&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">monitors for problems such as (a)&nbsp;</span>{{c1::peripheral nerve injuries}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">, (b)&nbsp;</span>{{c2::CNS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;lesions (eg. MS)</span>}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">, or (c)&nbsp;</span>{{c3::intraoperative monitoring (eg. spinal surgery)}}</div>"	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">during spinal cord surgery, loss of tibial nerve potentials with preservation of median nerve potentials can indicate nerve injury at the level of intervention. Anesthesia will affect&nbsp;</span>SSEP<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;potentials in both the upper and lower limbs</span></div>"										
"MS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;SSEP's are seen 90% of the time,&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">with the lower limb more likely to be abnormal than the upper limb.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">most common abnormality is the prolonged&nbsp;</span>{{c1::interpeak latencies}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">. Amplitude reduction or absence can also be seen</span></div>"	"<img src=""B9781437713695000296_f020-01-97814377136952.jpg"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">SSEP nerves most commonly used for testing are the&nbsp;</span>{{c1::median}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;for the upper limb and the&nbsp;</span>{{c1::tibial}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;nerve for the lower limb</span>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_52.png""><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_53.png""><br></div>"										
"SSEP's<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div>{{c1::are not::are / are not}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;considered useful for radiculopathies</span><br></div>"	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">The long pathway monitored can mask focal lesions between the recording sites, and&nbsp;</span><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">It monitors sensory pathways and proximal demyelinating injuries</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"

limbs</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">5–6 weeks</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Reinnervation begins</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">6 months to 1 year</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Increased amplitude from reinnervated motor unit. Reinnervation complete</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Every 3–4 months</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Serial&nbsp;EMG&nbsp;can be performed in intervals to monitor for reinnervation as clinically warranted</td></tr></tbody></table></div>"										
<b>Etiologies Demeylinating Injury</b><div><br></div><div>{{c1::Focal compression}} causing a transient ischemia or edema with {{c2::paranodal intussusceptions}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Chronic diseases causing degradation of myelin leading to {{c3::peripheral neuropathies}}</div>	"myelin invaginations<div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_15.png""><br></div>"										
"<b style="""">NCS</b>&nbsp;of demeylinating injuries <u>Latency</u> is typicaly {{c1::prolonged}} and <u>Amplitude</u> is typically {{c1::normal}}"	"<table><tbody><tr><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">NCS</th><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><br></th></tr></tbody><tbody><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Latency: <b>Prolonged</b><br><br>Conduction velocity: <b>Decreased</b><br><br>Temporal dispersion: Increased<br><br>Amplitude: May decrease secondary to&nbsp;<u>temporal dispersion </u>and<u> phase cancellation</u></td></tr></tbody></table><br><div><font color=""#fc0006"">Amplitude caveat</font>: may be decreased due to temporal dispersion or conduction block<br></div>"

axons&nbsp;</div><div><br></div>
<div>{{c1::duration}} of the AP is prolonged in
<u>temporal dispersion</u></div><div><br></div><div>causing, {{c1::<span style=""font-weight: 700; text-align: center;"">area&nbsp;</span>under the curve}}&nbsp;to remain the same&nbsp;</div>
</div>
</div>
</div></div>"	"<table><tbody><tr><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><span style=""font-weight: normal;"">not prolonged if the amplitude if truly</span> reduced 2/2 axonal injury<br></th><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""></th></tr></tbody><tbody><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1""><br><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-02-22 at 3.31.16 PM.png""><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-02-22 at 3.30.53 PM.png""><br>Demeylinating<br><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-21 at 10.18.40 AM.png""><br></td></tr></tbody></table>"

<div>For motor studies, amplitude should not decrease by
more than 20% on proximal stimulation (when compared to the distal amplitude).</div><div><br></div><div><u>Non-identical</u> waveforms may be secondary to accidental stimulation of <u>another
nerve</u>.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>ex. peroneal and tibial nerves are very close in the popliteal
fossa. If the <span style=""font-style: italic;"">pulse width </span>(duration of the stimulus) is increased, the wrong nerve may
be stimulated. Usually, the CMAP that results will have an initial positive (downward) deflection&nbsp;&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><img src=""mus27004-fig-0001-m.jpg""><br></div>
</div>

</div></div>"	For example, if the ankle plantar flexes, the tibial nerve is usually being stimulated

{{c3::axon or myelin}}, or both&nbsp;</div>

the SNAP will be affected&nbsp;<div><br></div><div><div>
<div>

of the CMAP may be affected, or it may be unobtainable.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>ex. motor neuropathy is
demyelinating, CMAP rmay have increased distal latency/
slowed conduction velocity&nbsp;</div><div><img src=""9780826134578_tab5_33.png""><br></div>
</div>
</div>

<div>Most peripheral neuropathies affect the {{c1::distal}} segment of the nerve&nbsp;</div>
</div>
</div>
</div></div>"	"more than the proximal segment<div><img src=""9780826134578_tab5_33.png""><br></div>"										
"

<div>EMG findings are usually {{c1::negative}} in peripheral neuropathy</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_tab5_33.png"">"										
<div>EMG findings are usually negative in peripheral neuropathy,&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>unless there is an {{c1::axonal motor neuropathy}}&nbsp;</div>	"In such cases (usually late stage), affected muscles may demonstrate spontaneous activity&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>EMG testing is helpful, even when negative, as it helps to rule out other disorders, such as a focal neuropathy or myopathy.&nbsp;</div><div><img src=""9780826134578_tab5_33.png""><br></div>"										
"
<div>
<div>
<div><div>{{c2::Uniform demyelination}}<span style=""font-style: italic;"">&nbsp;</span>– the entire length of the nerve displays a slower conduction
velocity.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>This is typically seen in dz's such as {{c1::Charcot–Marie–Tooth}} and {{c3::leukodystrophy}}&nbsp;</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>"	"and other hereditary disorders&nbsp;<div><img src=""9780826134578_tab5_33.png""><br></div>"										
"
<div>
<div>
<div><div><b>{{c1::Segmental demyelination}}<span style=""font-style: italic;"">&nbsp;</span></b>– uneven degree of demyelination of different nerve
fibers throughout the course of the nerve&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>which presents as&nbsp;{{c8::temporal dispersion}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><u>Dz example:</u></div><div>{{c2::AIDP / CIDP}}</div><div>{{c3::Arsenic}}</div><div>{{c4::MM}}</div><div>{{c5::AIDS}}</div><div>{{c6::LYME}}</div><div>{{c7::Leprosy}}&nbsp;</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>"	"For example, in the same nerve some fibers may be conducting at 50 meters/sec and some at 30 meters/sec. The sum will be a waveform that has lower amplitude but is more dispersed (wider)<div><br></div><div><b>CV slowed, CMAP amp low (2/2 dispersion, area is same)</b>&nbsp;<br><div><br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-02-22 at 3.31.16 PM.png""><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-02-22 at 3.30.44 PM.png""><br></div></div><div><img src=""9780826134578_tab5_33.png""><br></div>"										
"
<div>
<div>
<div><div><b>{{c1::Focal nerve slowing}}<span style=""font-style: italic;"">&nbsp;</span></b>– localized area of demyelination</div><div><br></div><div>which presents as a decrease in conduction velocity <b>{{c2::across}}</b> the lesion&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>ex. {{c3::cubital tunnel or entrapment neuropathy}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>usually evident if there is a more than {{c4::10}} m/s drop<br></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>"	"<div>
<div>
<div>
<div>
<div>In focal demyelination, only <b>one segment</b> of the nerve is affected.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Therefore, CV will be <u>normal</u> <span style=""font-style: italic;""><b>unless</b> </span>stimulation is <font color=""#fc0006"">across</font> the area of focal demyelination.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>(unlike axon and CB which are <b>ALL</b> proximal distal)</div><div><br></div><div>Latencies? and amplitudes should be normal&nbsp;</div></div></div></div></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-02-22 at 3.31.08 PM.png""><br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-02-22 at 3.30.44 PM.png""><img src=""Arrangement-for-motor-conduction-studies-of-the-ulnar-nerve.png""><br></div>"										
"
<div>
<div>
<div><div>{{c1::Conduction block}}<span style=""font-style: italic;"">&nbsp;</span>– an area of severe focal demyelination where AP cannot propagate.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>{{c2::decreased::nl or dec}}<span style=""font-style: italic;"">&nbsp;amplitude </span>with {{c3::proximal::proximal/distal}} stimulation&nbsp;</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>"	"<div>ex. CTS, saturday night palsy etc.</div><div><img src=""paste-adb55ab3021f3eeb1c533610e6b6276a0dedf522.jpg""><br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2021-10-21 at 10.05.19 AM.png""><br><div><br></div></div>"										
"<div>
<div>
<div>
<div>
<div>CMAP amplitude distal to a <u>conduction block</u> will be {{c1::unaffected::affected / unaffected}}&nbsp;</div>
</div>
</div>
</div></div>"	"CMAP obtained when stimulating proximal to lesion will have a lower amplitude.&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>However, when the nerve is stimulated distal to this area of compromise, the CMAP will be normal.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>This is because the axon itself has not been significantly compromised</div><div><img src=""paste-adb55ab3021f3eeb1c533610e6b6276a0dedf522.jpg""><br></div>"

<div>
<div>
<div>

"<b>Musculocutaneous n. course</b>&nbsp;<div><br></div><div><div>
<div>
<div>
<div>
<div>arises from
the lateral cord of the brachial plexus
near the lower border of {{c1::pectoralis
minor}} muscle.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>downward
to pierce the {{c2::coracobrachialis}} muscle,
which it innervates.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>in the upper arm, travels between the {{c3::brachialis and biceps::2}}
muscles&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>at the antecubital fossa,
it pierces deep fascia lateral to the {{c4::biceps tendon}} and becomes the LAC</div>

"<b>Axillary n.&nbsp;</b><strong>Course</strong>:<div><br></div><div>
<div>
<div>
<div>
<div>descends posterior to the {{c1::axillary}}&nbsp;artery&nbsp;and anterior to the {{c1::subscapularis}} muscle.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>it then curves posteriorly through the {{c2::quadrangular
space}} with the posterior circumflex artery.
</div><div><br></div>
<div>As the nerve emerges, it divides into anterior and posterior terminal divisions.&nbsp;</div></div></div></div></div>"	"<b>quadrilateral space:</b> capsule of the shoulder joint / teres minor above,&nbsp;<div>the surgical neck of the humerus laterally, the long head of the triceps medially,&nbsp;</div><div>and the teres major below.</div><div><br></div><div><div><b>posterior branch:</b> teres minor, posterior fibers of deltoid, and the upper lateral cutaneous nerve of the arm&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><b>anterior branch:</b> middle and anterior fibers of the deltoid</div></div><div><img src=""paste-cefef12f87c9a271885d8516f747478029ed0bef.jpg""><br></div><div><img src=""axillary-nerve.jpg""><br></div><div><img src=""DqSlhF2V4AA_KAz.jpg""><br></div>"

</div>

"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>suprascapular nerve. course</b>&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">originate from the C5 and C6 spinal nerve roots and&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">contributes to the&nbsp;</span>{{c1::upper trunk::plexus}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;which it branches off&nbsp;</span></div><div><br></div><div>then passes the {{c2::posterior triangle}} of the neck and runs beneath the {{c2::trapezius}} to the superior margin of the scapula.</div><div><br></div><div>It runs through the&nbsp;{{c3::<span style=""font-style: italic;"">suprascapular</span>&nbsp;notch}},&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">to innervate the&nbsp;</span>{{c5::supraspinatus}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>The nerve then wraps around the&nbsp;{{c4::<span style=""font-style: italic;"">spinoglenoid</span>&nbsp;notch}},&nbsp;to innervate the {{c5::infraspinatus}}</div>"	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2022-04-15 at 12.15.59 PM.png""><img src=""paste-fb15836675ccd362cbc78e1dbb7853899c388218.png""><img src=""CLD9Q7pBD9w5KQ0c9rGKyQ_suprascapular_nerve.png""><img src=""paste-86ef389d283a2cd9a740b65c8b1dee716e6e3a2f.jpg"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>SUPRASCAPULAR NEUROPATHY</b></span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b><br></b></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">This is the only peripheral nerve injury at the&nbsp;</span>{{c1::trunk}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;level.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">It is the most commonly involved nerve in&nbsp;</span>{{c2::neuralgic amyotrophy}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b><br></b></span></div>"	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">injured from trauma (forced scapular protraction), </span><font color=""#fc0006"">traction</font><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""> (from a massive rotator cuff tear), stinger/Erb’s palsy;&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">compression from </span><font color=""#fc0006"">spinoglenoid ganglions</font><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">, hematoma, suprascapular or spinoglenoid notch entrapment, or </span><font color=""#fc0006"">paralabral cyst.</font><br></div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_103.png""><img src=""Fig2.png"">"										
<div><i><b>Suprascapular neuropathy clinical pres.</b></i></div><div><br></div><div>proximal injury results in weakness in both {{c1::shoulder abduction (SS)}} and {{c1::external rotation (IS)}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Nerve injury at the spinoglenoid notch will result in weakness {{c1::only in external rotation&nbsp;(IS)}}</div>	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_104.png"">"										
"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>Long thoracic n.</b></span></div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>runs distally along the thoracic wall to innervate the&nbsp;</span>{{c1::serratus anterior}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">(</span>SALT<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;[</span><span style=""text-decoration-line: underline; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">S</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">erratus&nbsp;</span><span style=""text-decoration-line: underline; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">A</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">nterior&nbsp;</span><span style=""text-decoration-line: underline; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">L</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">ong&nbsp;</span><span style=""text-decoration-line: underline; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">T</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">horacic])</span><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-04-15 at 12.27.28 PM.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"										
<div>2 main types of shoulder winging.&nbsp; <u>EDx findings...</u></div><div><strong><br></strong></div><div><strong>Medial winging: </strong>EMG findings in<strong>&nbsp;</strong>{{c1::serratus anterior}}&nbsp;</div><div><strong><br></strong></div><div><strong>Lateral winging:</strong>&nbsp;EMG findings in {{c1::trapezius (&amp;SCM)}}</div>	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">nerve can be injured by traction from a fall,&nbsp;</span>MVA<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">, sports activities, or shoulder bags</span><div><div><div><br></div><div>Scapular Winging: Medial Versus Lateral Scapular Winging</div></div><table><tbody><tr><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">&nbsp;</th><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">MEDIAL SCAPULAR WINGING</th><th colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">LATERAL SCAPULAR WINGING</th></tr></tbody><tbody><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Nerve injury<br><br></td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Long thoracic nerve</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Spinal accessory nerve</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Affected muscle/function<br><br></td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Serratus anterior (Normal function: protracts and laterally rotates the scapula)</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Trapezius (Normal function: retracts and medially rotates the scapula)</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Position of scapula (Medial border)<br><br></td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Scapula retracted and elevated Medial scapular border closer to midline due to unopposed retraction from the trapezius</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Scapula protracted and depressed Medial scapular border is pulled away from midline by unopposed protraction from the serratus anterior</td></tr><tr><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Shoulder abduction causes</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Decreases winging</td><td colspan=""1"" rowspan=""1"">Increases winging</td></tr></tbody></table></div>"										
"<strong>Treatment of serratus anterior injury/injury to the long thoracic nerve</strong>: <font color=""#fc0006"">same 2 for both</font><div>(a) acute stage, pain reduction and&nbsp;ROM&nbsp;exercise;&nbsp;</div><div>(b) intermediate stage, <u>passive stretching</u> of the {{c1::rhomboids}}, {{c1::levator scapulae}}, and pectoralis minor;&nbsp;</div><div>(c) late stage, strengthening exercise of all shoulder girdle muscles, including the trapezius.</div><div><strong><br></strong></div><div><strong>Treatment of trapezius palsy/injury to the spinal accessory nerve</strong>:&nbsp;</div><div>Will involve physical therapy to adequately <u>strengthen</u> adjacent muscle groups, including {{c1::rhomboids}} and {{c1::levator scapulae}}.</div><div><br></div><div>Surgical repair with a {{c2::dynamic muscle transfer}} is recommended if the patient fails conservative treatment.</div>"

"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>lateral femoral cutaneous neuropathy</b> aka&nbsp;</span>{{c4::meralgia paresthetica}}<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><div><span style=""font-style: italic;""><u>Etiology</u></span></div><div><br></div><div>1.) {{c1::compression}}</div><div><br></div><div>2.) medical cuases: Diabetes, {{c2::tumor}}, infection, {{c2::weight gain/loss}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>3.) {{c3::Iatrogenic::category}}</div></div>"	"<div><span style=""font-style: italic;"">Etiology</span></div><div><br></div><div>chronic compression by a repeated low grade trauma: from a protuberant abdomen, pregnancy, or <u>tight clothing</u></div><div><br></div><div>Diabetes, tumor, infection, and rapid weight gain or weight loss can also affect the nerve.</div><div><br></div><div>Iatrogenic: incisions for lower abdominal/pelvic surgeries and laparoscopic <u>hernia repairs</u></div>"

"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">lateral femoral cutaneous nerve. <u>clinical pres.</u></span><div><br></div><div>patient may report sensory complaints in the lateral thigh, including pain, numbness, burning, or a dull ache,&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>exacerbated by {{c1::hip extension/flexion}} and {{c1::prolonged sitting}}</div>"	"<u>T<span style=""font-style: italic;"">reatment</span>:</u><div><br></div><div>Interventions may include rehabilitation,&nbsp;NSAIDs, Gabapentin, cortisone injections, surgical release.</div><div><br></div><div>Symptoms may be self-limited</div><div><br></div><div>In addition, removal of compressive clothing should occur (e.g., wide belt, compressive athletic clothing).</div>"

<b>Femoral Neuropathy,&nbsp;EDX&nbsp;findings:</b><div><br></div><div><u>NCS:</u></div><div>Abnormal {{c1::saphenous nerve&nbsp;SNAP}}</div><div>Abnormal&nbsp;{{c1::rectus femoris CMAP}}</div><div><br></div><div><u>EMG:</u></div><div>- Abnormal activity in femoral n. innervated m's&nbsp;</div><div>- if abnl, then study other m's (eg. {{c2::hamstrings, gluts, adductor::1ex.}}) to r/o {{c2::plexus/root::2}} involvement&nbsp;</div>	"EX. Involvement of obturator nerve innervated muscles (e.g., adductor longus) and/or lumbar paraspinals<div><br></div><div>could indicate an <b>L3/4 radiculopathy</b> over a femoral neuropathy</div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-07-16 at 8.58.50 AM.png""><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-07-29 at 8.34.33 PM.png""><br></div>"										
"{{c1::Diabetic amyotrophy}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is the most common cause of femoral neuropathy</span>"	"<b>a nerve disorder which is a complication of diabetes mellitus</b><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">.&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">It affects the thighs, hips, buttocks and legs, causing pain and&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">muscle wasting</span><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">It is also called by several other names, including proximal diabetic neuropathy, lumbosacral radiculoplexus, and femoral neurophagy</span></div><div><img src=""d6dYrT2IEzteiIf9FLspxA.jpg""><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);""><br></span></div>"										
"{{c1::Diabetic amyotrophy}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is a proximal diabetic neuropathy distinct from other types of distal diabetic peripheral neuropathies</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">it is also known as a&nbsp;</span>{{c2::lumbo-sacral radiculo-plexus::""4-names""}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;neuropathy</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">as it can involve the plexus and nerve roots, as well as peripheral nerves</span><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">It predominantly affects the lumbosacral plexus</span></div>"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">exact cause of <u>diabetic amyotrophy</u> is unknown&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">believed to result from a multifocal&nbsp;</span>{{c1::immune-mediated microvasculitis::2 names}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">The nerve is believed to be injured from an abnormality of the vaso-nervorum due to diabetes mellitus.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Nerve biopsy shows multifocal nerve fiber loss suggesting&nbsp;</span>{{c2::ischemic}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;injury and perivascular infiltrate</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">amyotrophy has been noted to occur after&nbsp;</span>{{c3::marked weight loss::pt characteristic}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"	"<img src=""ef50d63275392b7e1280045a3c08de88.jpg"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">diabetic amyotrophy&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">typically affects (epidimiology)</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div>{{c1::males}}<br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">usually&nbsp;</span>{{c1::&gt; 50 yo}}</div><div>{{c1::type 2 DM}}<br></div>"											
"<b>diabetic amyotrophy</b><div><br></div><div><div><u><span style=""font-style: italic;"">Clinical presentation</span>:</u></div><div><br></div><div>begins with {{c1::severe unilateral pain}} in the {{c2::lumbar region}} or {{c2::proximal lower extremity}}</div><div><br></div><div>commonly&nbsp;spreads to the&nbsp;{{c3::contralateral side}} within {{c3::weeks to months::time range}}</div>
<div><br></div><div>Patients then develops {{c4::weakness}} and {{c4::atrophy}} of the proximal &gt; distal lower extremity musculature</div></div>"	<div>typically associated <b>weight loss</b> that precedes symptoms.<br></div><div><div><br></div><div>patient may complain of asymmetric thigh pain, knee extension weakness (quadriceps), and atrophy.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Loss of the patellar reflex may also occur</div></div>										
"<b>diabetic amyotrophy</b>&nbsp;<b><span style=""font-style: italic;"">EDX&nbsp;findings</span>:</b><div><br></div><div><u>NCS:</u></div><div>{{c1::Abnormal}}&nbsp;SNAP saphenous*</div><div>{{c1::Abnormal}}&nbsp;CMAP rectus</div><div><br></div><div><u>EMG (Abnormal activity):</u></div><div>&nbsp;femoral innervated muscles&nbsp;</div><div>(±), {{c2::adductors}}</div><div>iliopsoas</div><div>{{c2::paraspinals}}</div>"	"<div>sounds like a <b><font color=""#0014ff"">L3/L4 radiculopathy</font></b></div><div><b><font color=""#0014ff"">* abnl sensory indicates plexus and not a radic</font></b></div><div><br></div><div>""hamstrings should be normal""</div><div><br></div><div><u>Treatment</u>:</div><div>Diabetic amyotrophy is a self-limited condition, but the recovery process is gradual and occurs over a period of months.&nbsp;</div><div>There are some patients who are left with residual lower extremity weakness.</div><div>Treatment is focused around pain control and optimizing glycemic control.&nbsp;</div><div>Physical therapy can assist in improving strength and functional mobility.</div>"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>SAPHENOUS NEUROPATHY</b></span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b><br></b></span></div><div><div><span style=""font-style: italic;""><u>Etiology</u></span></div><div><br></div><div>can be entrapped in the {{c2::hip adductor canal}} (aka {{c2::Hunter’s canal}}) or between the {{c3::sartorius}} and {{c3::gracilis}}</div><div><br></div><div>iatrogenic trauma, including {{c1::knee arthroscopy/meniscectomy}} or {{c4::catheterization/thrombectomy}}</div></div>"	"<img src=""Anatomy-of-the-adductor-canal.jpeg""><div><img src=""EGBaocEWkAA4k2h.jpg""><br></div>"										
"<b>Saphenous Neuropathy,&nbsp;</b><span style=""font-style: italic;"">EDX&nbsp;findings</span>:<div><br></div><div><u>NCS</u></div><div>SNAP: {{c1::Abnormal saphenous nerve}}</div><div>CMAP: {{c1::Normal}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><u>EMG</u></div><div>femoral nerve innervated muscles: {{c1::Normal}}</div>"	"Treatment: Interventions may include rehabilitation or surgical procedure<div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-07-16 at 8.58.50 AM.png""><br></div>"										
"<b>Sciatic Nerve, course </b>(tibial &amp; peroneal)&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>L4, L5 roots from the {{c7::lumbosacral trunk}}, and the 1st, 2nd, and 3rd sacral ventral rami<br><div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">exits the pelvis through the&nbsp;</span>{{c1::greater sciatic foramen}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span>below the {{c4::piriformis}}<span style=""font-style: italic;"">&nbsp;</span>muscle</div><div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">between the&nbsp;</span>{{c2::lesser trochanter}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;and&nbsp;</span>{{c2::ischial tuberosity}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">. (bony landmarks)</span><br></div><div><br></div><div>the nerve is deep to the {{c5::gluteus maximus::pelvis}} m. and {{c5::biceps femoris::thigh}} m.<br></div><div><br></div><div>down the midline of the thigh closely related to the {{c6::shaft of the femur}}</div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">travels as one unit up to the&nbsp;</span>{{c3::popliteal fossa}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">, where it splits into the peroneal (fibular) division and tibial division</span></div></div>"	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2022-07-16 at 9.23.52 AM.png""><div><img src=""images-6c4a4066b13b4da7c9a901e7cc25d3333a96cd39.jpg""><img src=""images-bb3090794b1688472f8fd3c74d88c130822b0dd6.jpg""></div><div><img src=""Posterior-View-of-the-Lower-Limb-Anatomical-Course-of-the-Sciatic-Nerve.jpg""><div><img src=""4KSllH4FY6mzJvkDtSJqZA_b.png""><br></div></div>"										
<b>Sciatic nerve</b> muscle innervation in the thigh<div><br></div><div><u>peroneal (fibular) division</u>&nbsp;</div><div>{{c1::Short head biceps femoris}}</div><div><u>tibial division</u>&nbsp;</div><div>{{c1::Long head biceps femoris}}</div><div>{{c1::Semitendinosus}}</div><div>{{c1::Semimembranosus}}</div><div>{{c1::Adductor magnus (also obturator n.)}}</div>	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2022-07-16 at 9.30.51 AM.png""><img src=""Figure0484-sciatic-nerve.jpg"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">the&nbsp;</span>{{c1::peroneal}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;division makes up the <u>outer</u> two-thirds of the sciatic nerve proper</span>"	"<img src=""f145-02-9780323549479.jpg"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>SCIATIC NEUROPATHY</b></span><div><font color=""#333333""><b><br></b></font><div><u>Etiology:</u></div><div>{{c1::hip dislocation / fx}}</div><div>{{c2::THA}}</div><div>{{c3::IM injection}}</div><div>hematoma / tumor&nbsp;</div><div>penetrating wounds<br></div><div>gravid uterus</div></div>"											
"{{c1::Piriformis syndrome}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is an uncommon type of compressive <u>sciatic neuropathy</u> at the pelvic outlet&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">that mainly affects the&nbsp;</span>{{c2::peroneal (fibular)}}&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">portion of the nerve </span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Because there is no consensus on diagnosing piriformis syndrome, it is a <b>dx of exclusion</b></span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">estimated incidence is approximately 4%</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_110.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"										
"<b>Sciatic neuropathy</b><div><span style=""font-style: italic;""><br></span></div><div><u><span style=""font-style: italic;"">Clinical presentation</span>:</u></div><div><br></div><div>primarily presents as weakness of {{c1::knee flexion}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>and {{c1::muscles of the peroneal (foot drop) and tibial nerves<font color=""#0014ff"" style=""font-weight: bold;"">* </font>(plantar flexion)}}</div><div><br></div><div>numbness occurs over the {{c2::lateral leg}} and the {{c2::entire foot}}</div><div><br></div><div>The {{c3::lateral hamstring}} and {{c3::Achilles reflexes}} may be abnormal (physical examination)</div>"	"<div><b>Motor =</b> hamstrings + foot drop (peroneal) + plantar flexion (gastroc)</div>pt c/o <font color=""#0014ff"">depends on which portion of the nerve is more involved</font> (can be peroneal alone)&nbsp;<div><b>Sensory =</b> peroneal + sural<br><div><img src=""400px-Gray826and831.PNG""><br><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_109.png""><br></div></div></div>"										
"<b>Sciatic neuropathy&nbsp;<span style=""font-style: italic;"">EDX&nbsp;findings</span>:</b><div><br></div><div><u>NCS</u></div><div>SNAP: Abnormal {{c2:: superficial peroneal (fibular) and sural sensory}}&nbsp;</div><div>CMAP: Abnormal {{c2::tibial and comm. peroneal (fibular) motor studies}}&nbsp;&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><u>EMG</u></div><div>Abnormal activity in {{c1::<u>all</u> sciatic innervated musculature&nbsp;</div><div>1.) hamstrings (eg. biceps femoris s/l + semi m/t),&nbsp;</div><div>2.) tibial n. (eg. gastroc + tib post), and&nbsp;</div><div>3.) c. peroneal n. (tib ant. + fib brevis/long)}}</div><div><br></div><div>Normal activity in {{c5::gluteus medius (r/o plexopathy)}} and&nbsp;</div><div>{{c5::lumbar paraspinals (r/o radiculopathy)}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>absent or delayed {{c4::H-reflex}}</div>"	"**even if sciatic is injured in the thigh --&gt; can be specificaly tibial or peroneal&nbsp;<div><img src=""Fh_22aeXgAEQJuU.png""><br><div><img src=""Sacral-Plexus-Deviation-of-the-Sciatic-Nerve.jpg""><br></div></div>"										
"{{c1::peroneal (fibular)}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;portion of the sciatic nerve is <u>more</u> vulnerable to injury&nbsp;</span>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">more vulnerable than the tibial because the peroneal portion is more fixated at the sciatic notch and at the fibula-neck. stretch</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">It has larger fascicles with less protective epineural tissue</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">and less blood supply&nbsp;</span></div><div><br></div><div>more exposed location&nbsp;</div>"

<div><b>Tibial nerve course</b>&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>descends along the popliteal fossa to
the distal border of the {{c1::popliteus}} muscle, superficial to it&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>proximally, it is positioned {{c3::lateral::side}} to the popliteal vessels, before crossing to the opposite side&nbsp;<br></div><div><br></div><div>passes anterior to the {{c2::aponeurotic arch::landmark}}&nbsp;</div><div>deep to the {{c2::soleus}} muscle, to enter the leg</div><div><br></div>
<div>in
the distal one-third of the leg it is covered only by skin and fascia, sometimes overlapped
by the {{c4::flexor hallucis longus}}</div><div><br></div><div>It reaches the {{c5::medial malleolus::bony structure}}, ending under the {{c5::flexor retinaculum}}</div><div><br></div><div>where it divides into medial and lateral {{c6::plantar}} nerves<br></div>
</div>

"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">DEEP PERONEAL (FIBULAR) NEUROPATHY</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">AKA&nbsp;</span>{{c1::anterior tarsal tunnel syndrome}}<span style=""font-style: italic; color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">refers to entrapment of the deep peroneal (fibular) nerve under the&nbsp;</span>{{c2::inferior extensor retinaculum}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;of the ankle</span></div>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_117.png"">"

Ant.}}</div>"	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2022-07-24 at 6.39.47 PM.png""><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-07-24 at 6.39.02 PM.png"">"

"<u>Peripheral Neuropathies</u> categorized based on distribution effected&nbsp;<div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">they can be described as&nbsp;</span>{{c1::diffuse}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;or&nbsp;</span>{{c1::multifocal}}<br></div>"	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2022-08-18 at 9.00.42 PM.png"">"										
<b>Inherited Peripheral Neuropathies</b><div><br></div><div><div><u>typically categorized as</u>:</div><div><br></div><div>{{c1::Hereditary motor and sensory neuropathies (HMSN)}}</div><div>{{c1::Hereditary sensory and autonomic neuropathies (HSAN)}}</div><div>{{c1::Hereditary motor neuropathies (HMN)}}</div></div>	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">based on the presentation</span><div><font color=""#333333""><br></font><div><font color=""#333333"">s</font>ubclassification is based on inheritance pattern and&nbsp;EDX&nbsp;findings (demyelinating vs. axonal)</div><div><br></div><div>Specific gene mutation is also relevant</div></div>"										
"<b>{{c1::HMSN}}</b> aka<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><b>{{c2::Charcot–Marie–Tooth}}</b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>&nbsp;disease</b>&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">is the most commonly inherited peripheral polyneuropathy&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">due to duplication mutation of the&nbsp;</span>{{c3::PMP<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">-22</span>}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;gene, l</span><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">ocated within the chromosome&nbsp;</span>{{c4::17p11.<span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">&nbsp;</span>2}}</div>"	"<div><img src=""Screen Shot 2023-01-22 at 10.04.14 AM.png""><br></div><div><img src=""_-97328df270a674021480354e171ca3778c61280a.jpg""><br></div>"										
<b>Acquired Neuropathies</b><div><br></div><div><u>most commonly related to</u>:</div><div><br></div><div>{{c1::Diabetes mellitus (most common)}}</div><div>{{c1::Acute inflammatory demyelinating polyradiculopathy (AIDP)}}</div><div>{{c1::Medications}}</div>											
"Acquired Peripheral Neuropathies<div><br></div><div>{{c1::Demyelinating inflammatory neuropathies}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;can manifest as a polyradiculopathy</span><br></div>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">Polyradiculopathy refers to the condition where more than one spinal nerve root is affected</span>"										
<b>Clinical Presentation of Peripheral Polyneruopathies&nbsp;</b><div><br></div><div>A classic triad has been described presenting in the lower limbs &gt; upper limbs:</div><div><br></div><div>{{c1::Sensory changes in a stocking/glove distribution}}</div><div>{{c2::Distal weakness}}</div><div>{{c3::Diminished/absent&nbsp;Reflexes}}<br></div>											
<b>Clinical Presentation of Poly Neuropathies&nbsp;</b><div><br></div><div><div><u>acquired polyneuropathies</u>:</div><div>{{c1::Burning / Pain::sx}}</div><div>{{c1::Paresthesias::sx}}</div><div><br></div><div><u>inherited polyneuropathies</u>:</div><div>{{c2::Sensory loss::phys-ex/sx}}</div><div>{{c2::Ataxia::phys-ex}}</div><div>{{c2::muscle cramping::sx}}</div></div>											
"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">EMG/NCS</span></div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>diagnostic criteria for peripheral neuropathy consists of evaluating at least&nbsp;</span>{{c1::three limbs}}"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Abnormalities of&nbsp;</span>SNAPs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">,&nbsp;</span>CMAPs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">, and&nbsp;</span>MUAPs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;are dependent on the type and timing of the pathology affecting a nerve</span><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-08-18 at 9.28.20 PM.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"										
"<b>Peripheral Neuropathy</b><div><br></div><div><u>EDX&nbsp;abnormalities can include</u>:</div><div>Prolonged latencies (o/l)</div><div>Increased conduction velocities (CV)</div><div>Reduced or absent amplitudes (uv)</div><div>Decreased {{c1::persistence}} (“missing” waveforms on {{c3::repetitive::same}} stimulations)</div><div>Increased {{c2::chronodispersion}} (large latency difference between the fastest and slowest waveform on {{c3::repetitive::same}} stimulation ""duration"")</div>"	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2022-08-18 at 9.28.20 PM.png"">"										
<b>Ddx Foot Drop</b><div><br></div><div>{{c1::Central: Tumor, cerebrovascular accident (CVA), arteriovenous malformation (AVM), spinal cord injury (SCI)}}<br></div><div>{{c2::Radiculopathy: L4–L5::2}}<br></div><div>{{c3::Plexopathy}}<br></div><div>{{c4::Mononeuropathy: peroneal (fibular) portion of the sciatic nerve, common peroneal (fibular), deep peroneal (fibular)::3}}</div><div>{{c5::Diffuse polyneuropathy: Diabetes}}</div>	"<img src=""foot-drop-physical-therapy-2696046-FINAL-a48944d48823462f821d0c443400e1c6.png""><div><img src=""https://www.researchgate.net/profile/Amie-Hoefnagel/publication/289965142/figure/tbl6/AS:668522229293063@1536399528436/Differential-diagnosis-of-foot-drop.png""><br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2023-01-11 at 11.37.35 PM.png""><br></div>"

"<b>HMSN<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51); font-weight: 600;"">I: CHARCOT-MARIE-TOOTH Edx Findings</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51); font-weight: 600;""><br></span></div><div><u>NCS</u></div><div>SNAP: Abnormal</div><div>CMAP: Abnormal,&nbsp;CV&nbsp;decreased by {{c1::70}}%</div><div>No {{c2::temporal dispersion}}</div><div>No {{c2::conduction block}}<br></div><div>No {{c2::focal slowing (diffuse slowing}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><u>EMG</u></div><div>{{c3::Normal}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51); font-weight: 600;""><br></span></div>"	"<img src=""9780826134578_ufig1.png"">&nbsp;CMAP<div><br></div><div>*temporal dispersion and CB are indicative of an aquired neuropathy&nbsp;</div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2022-08-18 at 9.28.20 PM.png""><br></div>"										
"<div><b>AIDP (GBS) and CIDP Edx findings</b></div><div><br></div><div><u>NCS</u></div><div><br></div><div>SNAP: {{c3::Abnormal}}</div><div><br></div><div>CMAP:</div><div>{{c3::Abnormal}} CV / o/p latecny</div><div>{{c3::normal (unless poor prognosis)}}: amplitude</div><div><br></div><div><u>NCS CMAP will be positive for</u>&nbsp;</div><div>{{c1::temporal dispersion}}</div><div>{{c1::conduction block}}</div><div>{{c1::focal slowing}}&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><div>{{c2::F-wave}}: {{c4::Abnormal—first&nbsp;EDX&nbsp;sign}}&nbsp;</div></div><div><br></div><div><u>EMG</u><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div><div>{{c3::typically Normal (unless axonal variant)}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><br></div>"	"<div><u>autoimmune response targets Schwann cells</u> (responsible for producing myelin sheath of peripheral nerves)<br></div>segmental demyelination throughout peripheral nerves<div><br></div><div>SNAP: absent or slowed</div><div>CMAP: increased distal latencies and slowed CV</div><div><br></div><div>EMG: normla, demeylinating</div><div>in most cases there is minimal or no axonal involvement, thus only see reduced recruitment&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>F wave tests the enitre lenght of the nerve</div><div>thus regular CMAPS can miss more patchy or proximal distribution of lesions&nbsp;</div><div>typically begins at the nerve roots ie <b>poly-radiculopathy</b></div><div><img src=""review-8639994442d3854049adcafccb16a83607e80f96.webp""><b><br></b></div>"

"<b>HIV<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">-Related Neuropathies</span></b><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><u>{{c1::Distal Symmetric Poly-neuropathy}}</u><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">:&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">most common type of neuropathy</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">primarily affects&nbsp;</span>{{c2::sensory}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;and&nbsp;</span>{{c2::autonomic}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;fibers</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">paresthesias begin in the&nbsp;</span>{{c3::toes}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;followed by the&nbsp;</span>{{c3::fingers}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2023-10-23 at 11.18.13 AM.png"">"										
"<b>NMJ</b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>&nbsp;disorders</b>&nbsp;</span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">hinder the production, release, or uptake of&nbsp;</span>ACh<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">a low&nbsp;</span>{{c1::safety factor}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;causes the amplitude of the&nbsp;</span>{{c2::endplate potentials}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;to fall below the threshold needed to generate a muscle fiber&nbsp;</span>AP</div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">This occurs due to an alteration of quantal response or content</span></div>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);""><b>safety factor:</b></span><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">&nbsp;</span>a measure of how much larger the endplate potential is compared to the threshold potential necessary to trigger an action potential&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>through the activation of voltage gated sodium channels</div><div><img src=""https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/cms/asset/1fee65cb-bdca-483b-853c-455c397f54fa/mfig004.jpg""><br></div>"										
"<div><strong>Myasthenia gravis</strong><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;(</span>MG<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">):&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">disorder resulting in a decreased quantal response due to an autoimmune response against postsynaptic&nbsp;</span>ACh<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;receptors</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">leads to&nbsp;</span>{{c2::reduced}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span>{{c1::<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">miniature endplate potential (</span>MEPP<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">)</span>}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span>amplitudes<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">, and&nbsp;</span>{{c2::normal}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;</span>frequency<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;(quantal content is normal)</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b><br></b></span></div>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>Postsynaptic membrane changes</b>.&nbsp;</span><div>MG<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">—Simplification of the postsynaptic membrane.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">The&nbsp;</span>NMJ<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;demonstrates a reduction in the number of postsynaptic junctional folds.&nbsp;</span></div><div>MS<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">—Hypertrophy of postsynaptic membrane; the&nbsp;</span>NMJs<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;demonstrate an increase in the complexity of the postsynaptic membrane architecture.</span><br><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_119.png""><br></div></div>"

"<b>Quantitative&nbsp;EMG</b><div><br></div><div>provides a more detailed measurement of the&nbsp;MUAPs.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It is a better indication of waveform {{c1::duration::same}}, which is a sensitive parameter for diagnosing {{c2::myopathies}}.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>The mean {{c1::duration::same}} is calculated using {{c3::20::#}}&nbsp;MUAPs&nbsp;and on a screen set with a trigger and delay line.&nbsp;</div>"	This avoids superimposing&nbsp;MUAPs&nbsp;and falsely creating a polyphasic.

<b>Myopathies</b><div><b><br></b></div><div><u>Single-Fiber&nbsp;EMG (may demonstrate):</u></div><div>{{c1::increased jitter}}</div><div>{{c1::increased fiber density (FD)}}</div><div>{{c1::increased blocking}}</div>	"<strong>Fiber density (FD;&nbsp;<a href=""https://connect.springerpub.com/content/book/978-0-8261-3457-8/chapter/ch05#fig5_126"">Figure 5–126</a>)</strong>:<div><br></div><div>This represents the&nbsp;number of single fibers belonging to the same motor unit within the recording radius of the electrode. The&nbsp;FD&nbsp;is determined by dividing the number of single muscle fiber&nbsp;APs&nbsp;at 20 sites by 20.</div><div><br></div><div>A&nbsp;FD&nbsp;of 1.5 is normal. Higher than this represents a denervation and reinnervation process.</div>"

"<b>Motor Neuron Disease</b><div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">It is important to rule out treatable neuropathies that mimic motor neuron disease (</span>MND<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">).&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">An example of this is&nbsp;</span>{{c1::multifocal motor neuropathy}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">, which includes conduction block and temporal dispersion, not seen in&nbsp;</span>MND<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">.</span><br></div>"	"<div><h2>What is multifocal motor neuropathy?</h2><div>a progressive muscle disorder characterized by weakness in the hands,&nbsp;</div><div>with differences from one side of the body to the other&nbsp;</div><div>It affects men much more than women.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><u>Symptoms also include:</u></div><div>-&nbsp;Muscle wasting</div><div>- Cramping</div><div>- Involuntary contractions or twitching of the leg muscles</div><div><br></div><div>The disorder is sometimes mistaken for amyotrophic lateral sclerosis (ALS),</div><div>But unlike ALS, multifocal motor neuropathy is treatable. An early and accurate diagnosis allows individuals to recover quickly.</div><div>treatment generally consists of intravenous immunoglobulin (IVIg) or immunosuppressive therapy with cyclophosphamide.</div><div>Improvement in muscle strength usually begins within three to six weeks after treatment is started.&nbsp;</div><div>Most who receive treatment early experience little, if any, disability.&nbsp;</div><div>However, there is evidence of slow progression over many years.</div></div><div><img src=""9780826134578_tab5_33.png""><br></div>"
