<b>CNS disorders Edx Findings</b><div><br></div><div>In&nbsp;CNS&nbsp;disorders, sensory and motor&nbsp;NCSs&nbsp;are normal.</div><div><br></div><div>On needle&nbsp;EMG, there is no denervation or reinnervation on the weak limb(s);&nbsp;</div><div>it reveals normal spontaneous activity and normal&nbsp;MUAP&nbsp;morphology.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>On voluntary contraction, recruitment is {{c1::normal}}</div>	<div>On voluntary contraction, however, the interference pattern is not complete due to decreased activation (i.e., decreased firing frequency);&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>the number of available&nbsp;MUAPs&nbsp;(i.e., recruitment) remains normal.<br></div>										
<b>SCI edx findings</b>&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>will EMG be abdnormal: {{c1::yes (at the level of the lesion)}}</div>	In a segmental&nbsp;spinal cord lesion, muscle innervated below the level of lesion will display the typical pattern of&nbsp;CNS&nbsp;lesion (i.e., decreased activation).&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>At the segmental level of the lesion, anterior horn cells may be affected, leading to a neuropathic pattern in muscles innervated by that segment.</div>										
<b>paraneoplastic neurologic syndromes&nbsp;(PNS)</b><div><br></div><div><u>related cancers</u></div><div>small cell lung cancer&nbsp;</div><div>{{c1::lymphoma}}</div><div>{{c1::myeloma}}</div>	paraneoplastic neurologic syndromes&nbsp;(PNS) result from immune cross-reactivity between tumor cells and components of the nervous system.<div><br></div><div>Paraneoplastic Syndrome are&nbsp;detected before cancer is diagnosed in 80% of cases.</div><div><br></div><div>Although Paraneoplastic Syndrome&nbsp;are rare, affecting &lt;1% of cancer patients overall,&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>certain malignancies have a substantially higher incidence of these conditions.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Up to 5% of patients with small cell lung cancer and up to 10% of patients with lymphoma or myeloma develop Paraneoplastic Syndrome.</div>										
"Paraneoplastic Syndrome can&nbsp;affect the&nbsp;CNS&nbsp;e.g.<div><br></div><div>{{c1::limbic encephalitis&nbsp;<span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">(hippocampus and amygdala)</span>}} and paraneoplastic {{c2::cerebellar degeneration}}</div>"	"can&nbsp;affect...<div><br><div>the&nbsp;NMJ&nbsp;(e.g., Lambert–Eaton myasthenia syndrome and myasthenia gravis),&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>the peripheral nervous system (e.g., autonomic neuropathy and subacute sensory neuropathy).<div><br></div><div>The diagnosis of&nbsp;PNS&nbsp;may incorporate imaging, serologies,&nbsp;EEG,&nbsp;NCSs,&nbsp;EMG, and cerebrospinal fluid analysis.</div><div><br></div><div>Because most patients&nbsp;diagnosed as having an apparent&nbsp;PNS&nbsp;will not have known cancer at the time, screening for an underlying tumor is indicated.</div><div><br></div><div>Immunosuppressive therapy is&nbsp;a mainstay of&nbsp;PNS&nbsp;treatment, but success is variable.</div></div></div><div><img src=""F2.medium.gif""><br></div>"

"<div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>Repetitive nerve stimulation:</b></span></div><div><br></div><div>These are studies&nbsp;in which a {{c1::repeated}} {{c1::supramaximal}} stimulation of a motor nerve is performed.</div><div><br></div><div>A series of&nbsp;CMAPs&nbsp;are recorded and evaluated for pathologic {{c2::amplitude changes}}.&nbsp;</div>"	"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Repetitive nerve stimulation: normal response</span><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_121.png""><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div>"										
"<div><b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Repetitive Nerve Stimulation&nbsp;</span></b></div><div><b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></b></div><div><u><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">(</span>RNS)&nbsp;SETUP</u></div><div>{{c5::Immobilize}} the electrode</div><div>{{c5::Immobilize}} the limb</div><div>Stimulate at a&nbsp;supramaximal level</div><div>Optimize limb temperature&nbsp;(approximately {{c4::30°C}})</div><div>Minimize {{c1::electrode gel}}</div><div>Stop {{c2::anticholinesterase inhibitors}}</div><div>Muscles should be evaluated in a {{c3::distal to proximal}} progression (if an abnormality is suspected but not demonstrated)</div>"	"<div>The study is&nbsp;best performed on the clinically weak muscle(s).&nbsp;</div><div>However, due to the ease of the examination, it is typically started in the hand intrinsics.&nbsp;</div><div>If no abnormality is noted, then progression to more proximal muscles is performed.</div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2024-01-18 at 2.23.01 PM.png""><br></div>"										
"<b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">Repetitive Nerve Stimulation&nbsp;</span></b><div><b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></b></div><div><u>ABNORMALITY</u><div>A &gt;{{c1::10}}% decrease&nbsp;in amplitude from the {{c2::1st}} to {{c2::5th}} waveform is significant for pathology</div></div>"											
<b>Low-Rate Repetitive Stimulation:</b><div><br></div><div>This repetitive stimulation&nbsp;test is performed at a rate of {{c1::2}} to {{c1::3}} Hz</div><div><br></div><div>Each stimulus causes&nbsp;the&nbsp;{{c2::EPP}}&nbsp;amplitude to drop.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>If the {{c2::safety factor}} is decreased, the potential will fall below the threshold necessary for activation.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>This results in a decrease of the&nbsp;{{c3::MUAP}}&nbsp;amplitude&nbsp;</div>	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_122.png"">"										
<b>Low-Rate Repetitive Stimulation:</b><div><br></div><div>An abnormality is&nbsp;considered when a&nbsp;CMAP&nbsp;demonstrates &gt;{{c1::10}}% amplitude reduction between the {{c2::1st}} and {{c2::4th}} waveforms</div><div><br></div><div>An increase in&nbsp;waveform can be seen if more stimulations are provided due to mobilization of {{c3::secondary&nbsp;ACh&nbsp;stores}}</div><div><br></div><div>A typical {{c4::U-shaped}}&nbsp;decrement can be seen in myasthenia gravis</div>	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2024-01-18 at 2.28.21 PM.png""><div><img src=""jcm-10-01736-g003-550.jpg""><br></div>"										
<div><div><b>{{c1::Postactivation Facilitation (PAF)}}</b>:</div></div><div><br></div><div>After a decrement&nbsp;is noted with&nbsp;LRRS, a 30-60 second {{c2::isometric contraction}} or {{c3::tetany-producing}} stimulation (50 Hz) should be performed.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>demonstrates a repair in the&nbsp;CMAP&nbsp;amplitude with an immediate follow up&nbsp;LRRS&nbsp;because of an improvement in neuromuscular transmission.</div>	"<img src=""9780826134578_fig5_123.png"">"										
<div><div><b>{{c1::Postactivation Exhaustion (PAE)}}</b>:</div></div><div><br></div><div>This response is&nbsp;seen as a&nbsp;CMAP&nbsp;amplitude decreases.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It occurs with a&nbsp;{{c2::LRRS::same}}&nbsp;performed every {{c3::minute}} for {{c3::5 minutes}} after an initial 30-60-second isometric contraction</div><div><br></div><div>This test should be used if a {{c2::decrement}} is not seen with the initial&nbsp;{{c2::LRRS::same}}, but a diagnosis of a&nbsp;NMJ&nbsp;disorder is suspected</div>	"<div>The greatest drop off is between 2 and 4 minutes.&nbsp;<br></div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_123.png"">"										
<b>High-Rate Repetitive Stimulation:</b><div><br></div><div>repetitive stimulation&nbsp;test is performed at a rate of {{c1::10}} to {{c2::50}} Hz.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It causes an accumulation of calcium in the cell, which assists&nbsp;{{c3::ACh&nbsp;release}}&nbsp;and repairs the waveforms</div><div><br></div><div>typically performed if a patient is unable to perform a {{c4::30- to 60-second::time}} {{c4:: maximal isometric contraction}}&nbsp;</div>	"<div><div>High-rate repetitive stimulation.&nbsp;<strong>(I)</strong>&nbsp;Increment with 50 Hz stimulation.&nbsp;<strong>(II)</strong>&nbsp;Increment with voluntary contraction (50 Hz simulation/train of 50, femoral/rectus femoris, 500% facilitation).</div></div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_124.png"">"										
"<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>High-Rate Repetitive Stimulation</b></span><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><u>NMJ disease and Amplitude Changes</u></span><div>{{c1::LEMS}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;= 200%–300% increment</span><br></div><div>{{c1::MG}}<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;= Decrement demonstrated and partially repaired</span><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><br></span></div></div>"											
<b>Pseudofacilitation</b>&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>a&nbsp;normal reaction and demonstrates a progressive increase in&nbsp;{{c1::CMAP&nbsp;amplitude}}&nbsp;with&nbsp;HRRS&nbsp;or voluntary muscle contraction</div>	"<div>however, the duration will decrease. ths the amplitude is the same&nbsp;</div><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_125.png""><br></div>"										
<div><b>Pseudofacilitation</b><br></div><div><b><br></b></div><div>It represents a&nbsp;decrease in {{c1::temporal dispersion}} due to increased {{c2::synchronicity}} of muscle fiber contraction</div>	"<div>The waveforms produced maintain a constant area under the curve though the amplitude appears increased because the duration is decreased<br></div><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_125.png""><br></div>"										
<b>Single Fiber EMG</b><div><br></div><div>This is a&nbsp;study that monitors the parameters of single muscle fiber&nbsp;APs.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It is useful if {{c1::repetitive stimulation}}&nbsp;is normal (and an abnormal diagnosis is still suspected)</div>	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2024-04-28 at 4.50.31 PM.png""><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2024-04-28 at 4.50.48 PM.png""></div>"										
<b>Single Fiber EMG</b><div><b><br></b><div>SFEMG&nbsp;is the most sensitive test for&nbsp;{{c1::NMJ&nbsp;disorders}} but has low specificity</div><div><br></div><div>Abnormalities can also be&nbsp;associated with {{c2::motor neuron disorders}}, and {{c2::peripheral neuropathies}}</div></div>	"<img src=""Screen Shot 2024-04-28 at 4.50.31 PM.png""><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2024-04-28 at 4.50.48 PM.png""><br></div>"										
<b>Single Fiber EMG Paramters</b><div><strong><br></strong></div><div><u>Fiber density</u></div><div><br></div><div>represents the&nbsp;number of {{c1::single muscle fibers}} belonging to the same {{c1::motor unit}} within the recording radius of the electrode</div><div><br></div><div>A&nbsp;FD&nbsp;of {{c2::1.5::decimal}} is normal. Higher than this represents a {{c3::denervation and reinnervation}} process</div>	"<div><div>The&nbsp;FD&nbsp;is determined by dividing the number of single muscle fiber&nbsp;APs&nbsp;at 20 sites by 20.<br></div><div><br></div><div><strong>(A)</strong>&nbsp;Normal muscle (action potentials from 1 to 2 fibers recorded).&nbsp;</div><div><strong>(B)</strong>&nbsp;Reinnervation (action potentials from many fibers recorded).</div></div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_126.png"">"										
<b>Single Fiber EMG Paramters</b><div><b><br></b></div><div><div><u>{{c1::Jitter}}</u>:</div><div><br></div><div>caused by a increased delay in the {{c2::inter-potential}} {{c2::discharges}} of two muscle fibers belonging to the same motor unit (normally 10 to 60 μsec)&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Disorders of neuromuscular&nbsp;transmission affect the safety factor and cause a delay in the time for an&nbsp;EPP&nbsp;to reach threshold for a muscle fiber&nbsp;AP,&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Reinnervation through collateral sprouting after a nerve injury results in poor activation of the immature&nbsp;NMJs</div></div>	"<div>Single-fiber EMG&nbsp;recordings.&nbsp;<span style=""font-style: italic;"">Top</span>: Superimposed view.&nbsp;<span style=""font-style: italic;"">Bottom</span>: Rastered view.&nbsp;<strong>(A)</strong>&nbsp;Normal.&nbsp;<strong>(B)</strong>&nbsp;Increased jitter.&nbsp;<strong>(C)</strong>&nbsp;Increased jitter with blocking.</div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_127.png""><br>"										
<b>Single Fiber EMG parameters</b><div><br></div><div><div><u>{{c1::Blocking}}:</u></div><div><br></div><div>This is an&nbsp;abnormality that occurs when a single muscle fiber&nbsp;AP&nbsp;{{c3::fails to appear}}</div><div><br></div><div>It occurs if the jitter becomes &gt;{{c2::100}} μsec.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It typically resolves in approximately 1 to 3 months, after reinnervation is completed.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>However, the increased jitter may take approximately 6 months to resolve</div></div>	"<div>Single-fiber EMG&nbsp;recordings.&nbsp;<span style=""font-style: italic;"">Top</span>: Superimposed view.&nbsp;<span style=""font-style: italic;"">Bottom</span>: Rastered view.&nbsp;<strong>(A)</strong>&nbsp;Normal.&nbsp;<strong>(B)</strong>&nbsp;Increased jitter.&nbsp;<strong>(C)</strong>&nbsp;Increased jitter with blocking.</div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_127.png"">"										
<b>Critical Illness Neuropathy Edx Findings</b><div><br></div><div><u>NCS</u></div><div><br></div><div>SNAP:&nbsp;</div><div>{{c1::low/unobtainable}}: amplitude</div><div>{{c1::mild slowing}}: CV o/p latency</div><div><br></div><div><div>CMAP:&nbsp;</div><div>{{c1::low/unobtainable}}: amplitude</div><div>{{c1::mild slowing (primarily axonal)}}: CV o/p latency</div></div><div><br></div><div><u>EMG</u></div><div>{{c2::Fibs/sharps}} seen in {{c2::distal}} muscles</div><div>recruitment patter: {{c3::neuropathic (decreased with high frequency)}}</div>	<div><b>Sensory Motor Axonal Peripheral Poly Neuropathy&nbsp;</b></div><div><br></div>predominant axonal process, low amplitudes<div>only mild slowing&nbsp;</div>										
<b>Critical Illness Myopathy Edx Findings</b><div><br></div><div>in general will present exactly the same as {{c1::myopathies}}</div>	SNAP: normal, snesory fibers not affected<div>CMAP: normal, typically distal muscles are spared</div><div>EMG: short duration, low amplitude MUAP with early recruitment</div><div>spontaneous activity is evident</div>										
{{c1::Sympathetic skin response}}:<div><br></div><div>a means of evaluating the unmyelinated, {{c1::sympathetic::same}} nerve fibers of the&nbsp;PNS</div>	"For median nerve&nbsp;testing using standard electrodes, E-1 can be placed on the palm and E-2 on the dorsum of the hand.&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>The median nerve is stimulated at the wrist and elbow at the usual locations.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Stimulation occurs over several minutes, and irregular stimulus intervals are required to prevent nerve habituation.</div><div><br></div><div>The stimulus sources&nbsp;used are electrical, coughing, noises, breathing, or tactile.<br></div><div><br></div><div><img src=""getfile_article_fulltext.php""><br></div>"										
<strong><strong>Sinus arrhythmia study</strong>: aka</strong><b>&nbsp;{{c1::cardio-vagal innervation}}&nbsp;study&nbsp;</b><div><br></div><div>dependent on the normal {{c2::heart rate variations}} that occur with {{c2::respiration}} via parasympathetic activity<div><br></div><div>test consists&nbsp;of measuring the {{c3::R-R ratio}} with an&nbsp;{{c3::EKG}}&nbsp;machine attached to the amplifier of the&nbsp;EMG.</div></div>	"Loss of this&nbsp;sinus arrhythmia represents a denervation process<div><img src=""fig14.jpg""><br></div>"										
<b>{{c1::Valsalva ratio}}</b><strong>&nbsp;study:</strong><div><br></div><div>heart rate varies in response to changes in blood pressure and intrathoracic pressure via sympathetic and parasympathetic activity.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Four phases are measured using a standard&nbsp;EMG&nbsp;machine. The findings measured in Phase 2 and Phase 4 are used for monitoring.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>Phase 2 should demonstrate a heart rate increase, while Phase 4 should demonstrate a decrease in the normal population.</div>											
<div><strong>Anal sphincter activity</strong>:</div><div><br></div><div>EMG&nbsp;recording of the external anal sphincter has {{c1::continuous}} activity at rest.&nbsp;</div>	There is a brief contraction in response to rapid rectal distension,&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>and a preserved or increased activity during a prolonged substantial rectal distension during defecation in healthy adults.</div>										
<b>Autonomic Nerve Studies</b><div><strong><br></strong></div><div>{{c1::Norepinephrine synthesis and&nbsp;release}}</div><div>Sympathetic Skin Response</div><div>Sinus Arryhthmia</div><div>Valsalva Ratio</div><div>Anal Sphincter Activity</div><div></div>	<div>Norepinephrine is the&nbsp;primary neurotransmitter for postganglionic sympathetic adrenergic nerves. It is synthesized inside the nerve axon, stored within vesicles, then released by the nerve when an&nbsp;AP&nbsp;travels down the nerve. Following are the details for release and synthesis of norepinephrine:</div><div>- The amino acid&nbsp;tyrosine is transported into the sympathetic nerve axon.</div><div>- Tyrosine is converted&nbsp;to dihydroxyphenylalanine (DOPA) by tyrosine hydroxylase.</div><div>- DOPA&nbsp;is converted to dopamine by&nbsp;DOPA&nbsp;decarboxylase.</div><div>- Dopamine is transported&nbsp;into vesicles then converted to norepinephrine by dopamine b-hydroxylase.</div><div>- An&nbsp;AP&nbsp;traveling down the axon depolarizes the membrane and causes calcium to enter the axon.</div><div>- Increased intracellular calcium&nbsp;causes the vesicles to migrate to the axonal membrane and fuse with the membrane, which permits the norepinephrine to diffuse out of the vesicle into the extracellular space.</div><div>- The norepinephrine binds&nbsp;to the postjunctional receptor and stimulates the effector organ response.</div>										
<b>AIDP</b>&nbsp;<div><br></div><div><u>clinical presentation</u></div><div>sx's worst at {{c3::4 weeks::time}} after onset&nbsp;</div><div>{{c1::symmetric::symmetric/asymmetric}} ascending paralysis</div><div>{{c2::absent reflexes}}</div><div>{{c4::bulbar (bell's plasy)}} and {{c4::respiratory}} muscle may be affected&nbsp;</div><div>{{c5::autonomic dysfunction}}&nbsp;</div>	"<div>sensory symptoms are typically mild</div><div>pain in 66%</div><div>Autonomic: tachy, brady, Ortho-stasis, urinary retention, and ileus&nbsp;</div><img src=""review-8639994442d3854049adcafccb16a83607e80f96.webp"">"										
<b>CIDP can present identical to AIDP</b><div><b><br></b></div><div>CIDP should be considered:<b><br></b><div><br></div><div>If the disease progresses for more than {{c1::8 weeks}} or if {{c1::the patient relapses}}</div></div>	"<img src=""cidp-and-ncs-protocol-2-320.jpg""><div><img src=""maxresdefault-b517cc174f82004533c3aa31cd4d88c3ba60f48f.jpg""><br></div>"										
<b>{{c2::Multifocal Motor Neuropathy}}:&nbsp;</b><div><br></div><div>a chronic inflammatory neuropathy that presents as an {{c1::assymetric::symetric/assymetric}} {{c1::pure motor::sensory/motor/mixed}} disorder&nbsp;</div>	"<div>anti-GM antibodes</div><div>may present like ALS but without UMN signs&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">Multifocal motor neuropathy is&nbsp;</span><b>a progressive muscle disorder characterized by weakness in the hands, with differences from one side of the body to the other in the specific muscles involved</b><span style=""color: rgb(32, 33, 36);"">. It affects men much more than women. Symptoms also include: Muscle wasting. Cramping.</span><br></div><img src=""10-Figure1.1-1.png"">"										
"<strong>Firing Rate</strong>:<div><br></div><div>This is the number of times a {{c1:: MUAP&nbsp;fires per second}}.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It is expressed in {{c2::Hz}} and is calculated by dividing {{c3::1,000::#}} by the {{c3::interspike interval (II)}}.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>take care to look at the units and make sure you are using {{c3::msec}}<br></div>"	"FR&nbsp;= 1,000/II<div><br></div><div><div><div>Firing rate: 1,000/13 = approximately 75.</div></div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_70.png""><br></div>"										
<b>{{c3::Recruitment frequency (RF)}}:</b><div><br></div><div>this is defined as the&nbsp;{{c1::Firing Rate}}&nbsp;of the {{c1::1st&nbsp;MUAP}}&nbsp;when {{c1::a 2nd&nbsp;MUAP&nbsp;begins to fire}}</div><div><br></div><div>Values <u>above</u> normal (20 Hz or below) correlate with a {{c2::neuropathic}} process</div>	"It is initiated by an increase in the force of a contraction.&nbsp;<div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(42, 42, 42);"">In this example, it is ~12 Hz, the reciprocal of the recruitment interval, which is 85 ms.</span></div><div><font color=""#2a2a2a"">8.5 divisions x 10msec = 85</font></div><div><font color=""#2a2a2a"">1000 / 85 = 11.8<br></font><div><img src=""6901.jpg""><br><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2024-01-21 at 9.52.19 AM.png""><br></div><div><br></div><div><br></div></div></div>"										
<div><b>{{c1::Recruitment interval (RI)}}:</b></div><div><br></div><div>This is the {{c2::interspike interval (in milliseconds)}} between two discharges of the {{c2::(same)&nbsp;1st MUAP}}&nbsp;when {{c2::a second&nbsp;MUAP&nbsp;begins to fire}}.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It is initiated by an increase in the force of a contraction. Normal is considered approximately {{c3::100}} msec</div>	"<div><span style=""color: rgb(42, 42, 42);"">In this example, strip B</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(42, 42, 42);"">it is 85 ms</span><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(42, 42, 42);"">8.5 divisions&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(42, 42, 42);"">8.5 x 10msec</span></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(42, 42, 42);"">= 85 msec</span></div><img src=""6901tn.jpg""><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2024-01-21 at 9.52.19 AM.png""><br></div>"										
<strong>Decreased&nbsp;RI&nbsp;(Increased&nbsp;RF)</strong>:<div><br></div><div>would be consistent with a {{c1::neuropathic process}}</div>	"A loss of motor units restricts additional motor unit activation to increase contractile force.&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>This causes the first motor unit to fire more rapidly until a second motor unit finally joins in.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>This shortens the interval between successive&nbsp;MUAPs&nbsp;from one motor unit</div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2024-01-21 at 9.52.19 AM.png""><br></div>"										
<strong>Increased&nbsp;RI&nbsp;(Decreased&nbsp;RF)</strong>:<div><br></div><div>is consistent with a {{c1::myopathic process}}</div>	"A loss of muscle fibers causes a second motor unit to join in early to help increase contractile force.&nbsp;<div><br></div><div>This occurs before the first motor unit has the opportunity to increase its firing frequency.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>This lengthens the interval between successive&nbsp;MUAPs&nbsp;from one motor unit.<br><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2024-01-21 at 9.52.19 AM.png""><br></div></div>"										
"<b>{{c4::Recruitment ratio (RR)}}:</b><div><br></div><div>This has been used to represent recruitment capabilities, especially when a patient demonstrates difficulty in controlling a contractile force.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It is calculated by dividing the&nbsp;{{c1::Firing Rate}}&nbsp;of the {{c1::first&nbsp;MUAP}}&nbsp;by the {{c2::number of different&nbsp;MUAPs&nbsp;on the screen}}.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">The normal&nbsp;</span>RR<span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);"">&nbsp;is considered &lt;</span>{{c3::10}}<br></div>"	"ex. A motor unit firing at 10 Hz when two different&nbsp;MUAPs&nbsp;are viewed on the screen demonstrates an&nbsp;RR&nbsp;of 5.&nbsp;<div>10 Hz/2 different&nbsp;MUAP&nbsp;= 5.&nbsp;<div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_71.png""><br></div></div><div>In ex B = 6</div><div>1000/85 = ~12</div><div>12 / (2 different MUAP's) = 6</div><div><img src=""6901tn.jpg""><br></div>"										
"<b>{{c4::Interference}}</b><span style=""color: rgb(51, 51, 51);""><b>&nbsp;Patterns</b></span><div><br></div><div>This is a qualitative or quantitative description of the sequential appearance of&nbsp;MUAPs.</div><div><br></div><div>It is the electrical activity recorded from a muscle during {{c1::a maximum voluntary contraction}}.&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>It is composed of&nbsp;{{c2::recruitment}}&nbsp;plus&nbsp;{{c2::activation}}.</div><div><br></div><div>It can be decreased in&nbsp;{{c3::CNS&nbsp;diseases}} and {{c3::poor patient cooperation (pain,&nbsp;hysteria)}}.</div>"	"<b>Activation</b> is the ability of a motor unit to fire faster to produce a greater contractile force and is controlled by a central process.<div><br></div><div>if a patient is asked to generate a force and only a <u>few&nbsp;MUAPs</u>&nbsp;are seen while the <u>frequency (Hz) continues to remain low</u>,&nbsp;</div><div><br></div><div>it can indicate <font color=""#fc0507"">decreased activation</font> from and is not the result of abnormal recruitment.<br></div><div><img src=""9780826134578_fig5_72.png""><br></div><div><img src=""Screen Shot 2024-01-21 at 10.19.36 AM.png""><br></div>"
